وإن سلم فمتى استدل المجتهد بهذه الآية، لم يكن الإجماعُ مُنْعَقِداً ، فاستدلاله بها على ترتيب الباقي استدلال بلا دليل، وتمسك بمجرد زعمه لا بالإجماع. وبه يندفع ما يقال : إنَّ فعل المسح مذكور في القرآن، والفاء إنّما دخلت على الغسل لا المسح ، فيثبت منه وجوب تقديم الغسل على المسح ، ثم يثبت الترتيب بين البواقي ؛ لعدم القائل بالفصل.
[١] قوله : وإن سلم ؛ في إيراد كلمة : «إن» التي تستعمل غالباً في المشكوك إشارة إلى أن التسليم إنما هو على سبيل الفرض لا على سبيل الحقيقة، وبه يندفع ما يتوهم أن تسليم دلالة : فَاغْسِلُوا وُجُوهَكُمْ ) على تقديم غسل الوجه غير صحيح؛ لكونه مخالفاً للمذهب. [٢] قوله : فمتى استدل المجتهد ... الخ ؛ حاصله : أن الشافعي له ادعـى بـأنَّ الترتيب في جميع أركان الوضوء فرض، واستدل عليه بأن تقديم غسل الوجه ثابت بالآية، ويلزم منه وجوب الترتيب في الباقي ؛ لأنّ وجوب تقديم غسل الوجه وعدم وجوب ترتيب الباقي قول بالفصل، فإنا قائلون بوجوب الترتيب في الجميع وأنتم أيها الحنفية قائلون بعدمه في الجميع، فنحن وأنتم أجمعنا على وجوب المساواة بين جميع الأركان وجوداً أو عدماً ، فالقولُ بالفصل خرق للإجماع المركب بيننا وبينكم. وهذا يقتضي أن يوجد الإجماعُ المركب بيننا وبينه قبل هذا الاستدلال، وهو لا يوجد إلا أن يثبت مذهبه من وجوب الترتيب في الجميع قبل ذلك ؛ ليكون ذلك مع مذهبنا إجماعاً مركباً، مع أنه ليس كذلك، فإنّه يستدلّ على إثبات مذهبه بهذه الآية، فيكون ثبوت مذهبه موقوفاً على هذا الاستدلال، فلا يكون مذهبه ثابتاً قبل هذا الاستدلال، فلا يكون الإجماع منعقداً قبل ذلك.
وهذا معنى قول الشارح : فمتى استدل المجتهد - أي الشافعي ه – على إثباتِ مذهبه بهذه الآية، لم يكن الإجماع - أي المركب - بيننا وبينه منعقداً مع قطع النظر عن هذا الاستدلال.
وقد رأيت في كتبهم : الاستدلال بقولِهِ : هَذَا وُضُوءُ لَا يَقْبَلُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى الصَّلاةَ إلا به»
وبالجملة استدلاله المذكور موقوف على ثبوت الإجماع بيننا وبينه قبله، وهو موقوف على ثبوت مذهبه ،قبله، مع أنه يستدل عليه بالآية، فيلزم الدور لتوقف ثبوت مذهبه على هذا الاستدلال المتوقف على ثبوتِ الإجماع المركب، المتوقف على ثبوت مذهبه، والدليل المستلزم للدور باطل، فيكون دليله كلا دليل، فاستدلاله دعوى بلا دليل.
وهذا معنى قوله : «فاستدلاله»: أي ذلك المجتهد بها : أي هذه الآية على ترتيب الباقي استدلال بلا دليل ؛ لكون دليله في حكم العدم، وتمسك بمجرد زعمه - بضم الزاي المعجمة وبالفتح والكسر أيضاً - أي ظنه لا بالإجماع ؛ لعدم وجوده قبل ذلك. فإن قلت : هذا إنّما يَرِدُ لو كانت هذه الآية أوَّلُ ما استدل به الشافعي له على وجوب الترتيب، وإلا فيجوز أن يكون ذلك ثابتاً عنده بدليل آخر، فينعقد الإجماع بثبوتِ مذهبه قبل الاستدلال بهذه الآية، فيتم استدلاله بها.
قلت : فحينئذ لا يكون الاستدلال بالآية على النمط المذكور دليلاً مستقلاً وافياً، بل يكون محتاجاً إلى دليل آخر لإثبات مذهبه، وكلامنا على تقدير كون الاستدلال المذكور حجة مستقلة.
فإن قلت آخذاً من «الحواشي العصامية» وغيرها أن هذا الاستدلال ليس من المجتهد حتى يرد عليه ما أورد، بل من أتباعه إلزاماً للخصم. قلت : : على هذا التقدير أيضاً يرد الإيراد، فإنّ استدلال تابعي المجتهد موقوف على ثبوت الإجماع المركب قبله، المتوقف على ثبوت مذهب مجتهده ؛ أي وجوب الترتيب المتوقف على هذا الاستدلال، وفي المقام أبحاث أخر ذكرناها في «السعاية»(۱). [١]قوله : هذا وضوء ... الخ ؛ ذكر الزيلعي عبد الله بن يوسف له في «تخريج أحاديث الهداية»(۲) : إنَّ هذا الحديث أخرجه الدارقطني عن ابن عمر له قال : توضأ
Book of Purification: Wudu. (2) And if it is granted, then whenever the mujtahid uses this verse as evidence, the consensus (ijma') is not established. So his using it to prove order in the rest is evidence without proof, and clinging to mere assumption, not consensus. And by this is refuted what is said: that the act of wiping is mentioned in the Quran, and the letter fa only entered upon washing, not wiping, so from it is established the obligation of washing before wiping, then order is established among the rest because of the absence of one who says there is a distinction. [1] His saying: 'And if it is granted': in using the word 'in' which is mostly used for the doubtful, it indicates that the concession is only hypothetical, not real. And by this is refuted the misconception that conceding the implication of 'fa-ghsilu wujuhakum' for precedence of washing the face is invalid because it contradicts the school. [2] His saying: 'then whenever the mujtahid uses it...' etc.; its gist: that al-Shafi'i claimed that order in all pillars of wudu is fard, and he argued that precedence of washing the face is established by the verse, and from it follows the obligation of order in the rest, because obligation of washing the face first and non-obligation of order in the rest is a saying of distinction (qawl bi al-fasl). For we hold order in all, and you Hanafis hold non-order in all, so we and you have agreed on the necessity of equality among all pillars in existence or non-existence, so the saying of distinction violates the compound consensus between us and you. This requires that the compound consensus exist between us and him before this istidlal, and it does not exist unless his madhhab of obligatory order in all is established before that, so that together with our madhhab it becomes a compound consensus; but it is not so, for he uses this verse to prove his madhhab, so his madhhab's establishment depends on this istidlal, so his madhhab is not established before this istidlal, so consensus is not established before that. And this is the meaning of the commentator's saying: 'then whenever the mujtahid — i.e. al-Shafi'i — uses it to prove his madhhab, the consensus — i.e. the compound — between us and him is not established irrespective of this istidlal.' And I have seen in their books: the use of his saying: 'This is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer.' In summary, his aforementioned istidlal depends on the establishment of consensus between us and him before it, which depends on the establishment of his madhhab before it, while he uses the verse for it, so circularity arises because his madhhab's establishment depends on this istidlal, which depends on the establishment of compound consensus, which depends on his madhhab's establishment. And a proof that entails circularity is invalid, so his proof is no proof, so his istidlal is a claim without proof. And this is the meaning of his saying: 'So his istidlal': i.e. that mujtahid's using it, i.e. this verse, to prove order in the rest is an istidlal without proof, because his proof is in effect non-existent, and clinging to mere assumption — with a damma on the zay, and also with fatha and kasra — i.e. his conjecture, not to consensus, because it does not exist before that. If you say: This only arises if this verse was the first thing al-Shafi'i used to prove obligation of order; otherwise it is possible that it is established with him by another proof, so consensus is established by his madhhab being established before using this verse, so his istidlal with it is complete. I say: In that case, the istidlal with the verse in the aforementioned manner is not an independent and sufficient proof, but needs another proof to establish his madhhab, and our discussion is on the assumption that the mentioned istidlal is an independent proof. If you say, taking from al-Hawashi al-Isamiyyah and others, that this istidlal is not from the mujtahid himself so that the objection applies, but from his followers as a necessary consequence (ilzam) to the opponent. I say: On this assumption too the objection applies, because the istidlal of the follower of the mujtahid depends on the establishment of compound consensus before it, which depends on the establishment of his mujtahid's madhhab — i.e. obligation of order — which depends on this istidlal. And in this context there are other investigations which we have mentioned in al-Si'ayah. [1] His saying: 'This wudu...' etc.; al-Zayla'i 'Abd Allah ibn Yusuf mentioned in his Takhrij Ahadith al-Hidayah that this hadith was narrated by al-Daraqutni from Ibn 'Umar who said: he performed wudu.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute in which the Hanafi commentator refutes the Shafi'i argument for the obligation of order (tartib) in wudu. The Shafi'i position claims that order among all wudu limbs is obligatory (fard), citing the Quranic verse (5:6) which uses the conjunction 'fa' (then) to imply sequence, and then argues that since Hanafis also agree that washing the face precedes wiping the head (due to the fa), but do not extend order to all limbs, they are guilty of a 'qawl bi al-fasl' (saying of distinction) which violates a supposed 'compound consensus' (ijma' murakkab) between the two schools. The Hanafi commentator demonstrates that this argument entails circular reasoning (dawr): the Shafi'i madhhab must be established before the compound consensus can exist, but the Shafi'i uses the very consensus to prove his madhhab. The commentator also addresses potential counterarguments: (1) if the Shafi'i has another proof, then his istidlal with the verse is not independent; (2) if the argument is from followers as an ilzam (imposition), the same circularity applies. Finally, he notes a hadith cited by Shafi'is: 'This is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer', and refers to al-Zayla'i's takhrij. The overall refutation is logical, not based on textual proof, and shows that the Shafi'i argument cannot stand on its own.

Key Terms
الإجماع المركب (al-ijma' al-murakkab): A compound consensus where two parties agree on a general principle (e.g., all limbs are equal in ruling) but differ on its application to a specific case.
القول بالفصل (al-qawl bi al-fasl): Claiming a difference or distinction between two similar cases without clear evidence, leading to inconsistency.
الدور (al-dawr): Circular reasoning where the premise depends on the conclusion and vice versa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi commentator, why does the Shafi'i argument from 'compound consensus' (ijma' murakkab) fail?
A) Because the hadith cited by Shafi'is is weak (da'if).
B) Because the Shafi'i madhhab must be established before the consensus can exist, but the Shafi'i uses the verse to prove his madhhab, leading to circularity (dawr).
C) Because Hanafis accept order in all wudu actions, so there is no disagreement.
D) Because the Quranic verse explicitly contradicts the Shafi'i claim.

Key Takeaway
The Shafi'i argument for obligatory order in wudu based on compound consensus is invalid due to circular reasoning (dawr); the consensus cannot be formed without the very position being contested.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Refutation of the Shafi'i Proof for Fardiyyat al-Tartib in Wudu
Critical refutation of Shafi'i proof for fardiyyat al-tartib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof for tartib being fard, and identify the three refutations based on hadith weakness, ahad status, and lack of evidence for order.

Core Idea
A weak ahad hadith cannot prove fard; order in wudu is wajib, not fard.

The Shafi'i school argues that order (tartib) in wudu is fard (obligatory) based on a hadith where the Prophet said, "This is an ablution without which Allah does not accept prayer." The Hanafi commentator, however, refutes this claim by exposing circular reasoning in the Shafi'i argument and by critiquing the hadith itself. Let us examine this critique step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Shafi'i argument
The Shafi'i school claims that order in wudu is fard. They support this with a hadith where the Prophet performed wudu in order and said that prayer is not accepted without it. They also claim consensus (ijma') on this obligation.
2
Identify the circular reasoning
The commentator shows that the Shafi'i argument is circular: they claim consensus on the obligation of order, but their own proof for that obligation (the hadith) depends on accepting their school's position. Thus, the consensus is not independent.
This is known as dawr (circularity).
3
Analyze the hadith criticism
The hadith is examined: it is weak (da'if) in all its chains according to major hadith critics (al-Daraqutni, al-Bayhaqi, etc.). Even if authentic, it is a hadith ahad, which in Hanafi usul establishes only wajib, not fard.
4
Examine the third refutation
Even if the hadith were authentic, there is no evidence that the Prophet's wudu in that narration was performed in order. The hadith text does not mention order explicitly.
The claim of order is an assumption.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
Therefore, the Shafi'i proof fails. The Hanafi school holds that order in wudu is wajib (obligatory but from a zanni proof), not fard. Imam Abu Hanifa says wajib; the Sahibayn say sunnah, but the mufta bihi is wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد رأيت في كتبهم : الاستدلال بقولِهِ : هَذَا وُضُوءُ لَا يَقْبَلُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى الصَّلاةَ إلا به» وبالجملة استدلاله المذكور موقوف على ثبوت الإجماع بيننا وبينه قبله، وهو موقوف على ثبوت مذهبه ،قبله، مع أنه يستدل عليه بالآية، فيلزم الدور لتوقف ثبوت مذهبه على هذا الاستدلال المتوقف على ثبوتِ الإجماع المركب، المتوقف على ثبوت مذهبه، والدليل المستلزم للدور باطل، فيكون دليله كلا دليل، فاستدلاله دعوى بلا دليل. وهذا معنى قوله : «فاستدلاله»: أي ذلك المجتهد بها : أي هذه الآية على ترتيب الباقي استدلال بلا دليل ؛ لكون دليله في حكم العدم، وتمسك بمجرد زعمه - بضم الزاي المعجمة وبالفتح والكسر أيضاً - أي ظنه لا بالإجماع ؛ لعدم وجوده قبل ذلك. فإن قلت : هذا إنّما يَرِدُ لو كانت هذه الآية أوَّلُ ما استدل به الشافعي له على وجوب الترتيب، وإلا فيجوز أن يكون ذلك ثابتاً عنده بدليل آخر، فينعقد الإجماع بثبوتِ مذهبه قبل الاستدلال بهذه الآية، فيتم استدلاله بها. قلت : فحينئذ لا يكون الاستدلال بالآية على النمط المذكور دليلاً مستقلاً وافياً، بل يكون محتاجاً إلى دليل آخر لإثبات مذهبه، وكلامنا على تقدير كون الاستدلال المذكور حجة مستقلة. فإن قلت آخذاً من «الحواشي العصامية» وغيرها أن هذا الاستدلال ليس من المجتهد حتى يرد عليه ما أورد، بل من أتباعه إلزاماً للخصم. قلت : : على هذا التقدير أيضاً يرد الإيراد، فإنّ استدلال تابعي المجتهد موقوف على ثبوت الإجماع المركب قبله، المتوقف على ثبوت مذهب مجتهده ؛ أي وجوب الترتيب المتوقف على هذا الاستدلال، وفي المقام أبحاث أخر ذكرناها في «السعاية»(۱). [١]قوله : هذا وضوء ... الخ ؛ ذكر الزيلعي عبد الله بن يوسف له في «تخريج أحاديث الهداية»(۲) : إنَّ هذا الحديث أخرجه الدارقطني عن ابن عمر له قال : توضأ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مرة مرة ، وقال : «هذا وضوء لا يقبلُ الله صلاة إلا به ، ثم توضأ مرتين مرتين ، وقال : هذا وضوء من يضاعف له الأجر، ثم توضأ ثلاثاً ثلاثاً وقال : هذا وضوئي ووضوء المرسلين قبلي). وكذلك أخرجه البيهقي، وفي سنده المسيب بن واضح لا يحتج به، ونحوه أخرجه ابن ماجه والطبراني في معجمه الأوسط»، وابن حبّان في كتاب «الضعفاء»، والدارقطني في كتاب «غرائب مالك»، وفي جميع أسانيده ضعف، كما بسطه الزيلعي والحافظ ابن حجر، والنووي، وغيرهم. [١] قوله : فيفرض الترتيب ؛ حاصله : أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم توضأ مرة مرة ؛ أي غسل أعضاءه فيه مرة مرة ، وقال : هذا - أي الذي فعلته - لا يقبلُ الله الصلاة إلا به ، فحصر قبول الصلاة في مثل وضوئه، وقد كان وضوؤه ذلك مرتباً فيعلم منه أنه لا يقبلُ الله صلاة إلا بالوضوء المرتب، وما شأنه كذلك لا يكون إلا فرضاً، فيكون الترتيب فرضاً ، ويُرَدُّ هذا الاستدلال بوجوه : ۱. منها : إنّ الحديث بجميع طرقه ضعيف لا يصلح للاحتجاج به على افتراض شيء. ٢. ومنها : إنّه بعد صحته هو من أخبار الآحاد التي لا تثبت الافتراض. . ومنها : إن دعوى أن ذلك الوضوء كان مرتباً دعوى من غير بينة، فإنّه لم يرد في طرق الحديث المذكور ذلك، وليس في كتب الحديث، وما نقلوه في طريق من (۱) في سنن الدراقطني (۱) : (۷۹ ، ولفظه : عن ابن عمر ه: أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم دعا بماء فتوضا مرة مرة ، ثم قال هذا وظيفة الوضوء الذي لا يقبل الله الصلاة إلا به ، ثم دعا بماء فتوضاً مرتين مرتين، ثم سكت ساعة، ثم قال هذا وضوء من توضأ به كان له أجره مرتين ، ثم دعا بماء فتوضأ ثلاثاً ثلاثاً، ثم قال : هذا وضوئي ووضوء الأنبياء من قبلي»، وقريب منه في «سنن ابن ماجة»(١ : ١٤٥) ، و(مسند الشاشي (٤) : ٢٥٣) ، و(مسند أحمد (١٠: ٥٨)، و«المستدرك» (۱ : ٢٥۱) ، و(مسند الطيالسي (۳) (۱۱۳)، وغيرها. قال الوادياشي في «تحفة المحتاج»(۱ : ۱۸۹): «فيه ضعف وانقطاع، واستشهد به الحاكم».
I have seen in their books: the deduction by his saying: 'This is an ablution without which Allah the Exalted does not accept prayer.' In summary, his mentioned deduction depends on establishing consensus between us and him before it, and it depends on establishing his school before him, while he deduces from the verse, so circularity follows because the establishment of his school depends on this deduction, which depends on the establishment of composite consensus, which depends on the establishment of his school. The proof that entails circularity is invalid, so his proof is like no proof, thus his deduction is a claim without proof. And this is the meaning of his saying: 'So his deduction' meaning that mujtahid with it, i.e. this verse, on the order of the remaining is a deduction without proof because his proof is in the condition of non-existence, and he clings to mere his assumption - with dhamma of the dotted za and with fatha and kasra also - i.e. his opinion, not consensus, because it does not exist before that. If you say: This only applies if this verse was the first thing al-Shafi'i used to deduce for the obligation of order, otherwise it is possible that it is established with him by another proof, so consensus is concluded by the establishment of his school before deducing with this verse, so his deduction with it is valid. I say: Then the deduction with the verse in the mentioned manner is not an independent sufficient proof, but rather it needs another proof to establish his school, and our speech is on the assumption that the mentioned deduction is an independent proof. If you say, taking from 'al-Hawashi al-Isamiyyah' and others, that this deduction is not from the mujtahid so that the objection applies, but rather from his followers to impose on the opponent. I say: On this assumption, the objection also applies, because the deduction of the follower of the mujtahid depends on establishing the composite consensus before it, which depends on establishing the school of his mujtahid, i.e. the obligation of order, which depends on this deduction. And in this context are other investigations that we mentioned in 'al-Si'ayah'. His saying: 'This wudu... etc.'; al-Zayla'i Abdullah ibn Yusuf mentioned for him in 'Takhrij Ahadith al-Hidayah' that this hadith was narrated by al-Daraqutni from Ibn Umar who said: The Messenger of Allah performed wudu once once, and said: 'This is an ablution without which Allah does not accept prayer', then he performed wudu twice twice, and said: 'This is an ablution for which the reward is doubled', then he performed wudu three times three, and said: 'This is my ablution and the ablution of the messengers before me.' Similarly, al-Bayhaqi narrated it, and in its chain is al-Musayyib ibn Wadih who is not authoritative, and similar was narrated by Ibn Majah and al-Tabarani in his al-Mu'jam al-Awsat, and Ibn Hibban in his book al-Du'afa, and al-Daraqutni in his book Ghara'ib Malik, and in all its chains there is weakness, as detailed by al-Zayla'i, al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar, al-Nawawi, and others. His saying: 'Thus order is made obligatory'; its summary: The Prophet performed wudu once once, i.e. he washed his limbs in it once once, and said: 'This - i.e. what I did - Allah does not accept prayer except with it', so he confined acceptance of prayer to the like of his wudu, and his wudu was ordered, so it is known from it that Allah does not accept prayer except with ordered wudu, and what is like that is nothing but obligatory, so order becomes obligatory. And this deduction is refuted in several ways: 1. Among them: The hadith in all its chains is weak, not fit to be used as proof for making something obligatory. 2. Among them: Even if it were authentic, it is from ahad narrations which do not establish obligation. 3. Among them: The claim that that wudu was ordered is a claim without evidence, for that is not mentioned in the chains of the hadith mentioned, nor is it in hadith books. And what they narrated in some chains? (Footnote: In Sunan al-Daraqutni (1): 79, with wording: From Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah called for water and performed wudu once once, then said 'This is the function of wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer', then he called for water and performed wudu twice twice, then was silent for a while, then said 'This is the wudu of one who performs wudu and gets his reward twice', then he called for water and performed wudu three times three, then said 'This is my wudu and the wudu of the prophets before me.' Similar in Sunan Ibn Majah (1:145), Musnad al-Shashi (4:253), Musnad Ahmad (10:58), al-Mustadrak (1:251), Musnad al-Tayalisi (3:113), and others. Al-Wadiashi said in Tuhfat al-Muhtaj (1:189): 'There is weakness and disconnection in it, and al-Hakim used it as evidence.'
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from the Hanafi commentary 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on Sharh al-Wiqayah. The author addresses the Shafi'i school's use of a hadith to prove that order (tartib) in wudu is obligatory (fard). The commentary begins by exposing circular reasoning (dawr) in the Shafi'i argument: they claim consensus on the obligation of order, but that consensus depends on their own ruling, which they try to prove using the same hadith. This makes the argument circular and thus invalid. The author then discusses a possible objection: what if the Shafi'i had another proof before using this hadith? He responds that then the hadith alone is not an independent proof. Even if the argument is from followers, not from al-Shafi'i himself, the circularity remains. Next, the hadith is quoted in detail, along with its chains, all of which are weak (da'if) according to major hadith critics like al-Zayla'i, Ibn Hajar, and al-Nawawi. The commentary then explains how the opposing school uses the hadith: the Prophet's wudu was ordered, and he said 'Allah does not accept prayer except with it', so order must be obligatory. Three refutations are given: (1) The hadith is weak in all its chains and cannot be used for establishing an obligation. (2) Even if authentic, it is a hadith ahad, and according to the Hanafi usul principle, ahad hadith do not establish fard (obligation) but only wajib. (3) The claim that the Prophet's wudu in that hadith was ordered is unproven; the hadith texts do not mention that the order was observed. Throughout, the Hanafi position is upheld: order in wudu is wajib, not fard.

Key Terms
ترتيب (tartib): Performing the actions of wudu in the prescribed sequence: hands, mouth, nose, face, arms, wiping head, ears, feet.
فَرْض (fard): A religious obligation established by a definitive proof (Quran, mutawatir sunnah, or ijma).
إجماع مركب (ijma' murakkab): Consensus that depends on a prior agreement on a subsidiary ruling; here, the consensus on tartib depends on the Shafi'i school's position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis not accept the hadith 'هذا وضوء لا يقبل الله صلاة إلا به' as proof that order in wudu is fard?
A) Because the hadith contradicts the Quran.
B) Because the hadith is weak and even if authentic, it is ahad and cannot establish fard.
C) Because the Prophet performed wudu without order sometimes.
D) Because the hadith was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
Order in wudu is wajib according to the Hanafi school, not fard, because the Shafi'i hadith is weak and ahad, lacking the strength to impose a fard obligation.

Hanafi Refutation of the Hadith for Wudu Order
Refutation of the hadith for tartib as fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that tartib is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard, by critically analyzing the hadith 'هذا وضوء لا يقبل الله صلاة إلا به' using hadith criticism and usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
A weak hadith cannot turn a sunnah into a fard; a pronoun's reference is limited.

In this lesson, we examine the classical inter-madhhab dispute over whether performing wudu in order (tartib) is obligatory (fard). The Shafi'i school relies on a hadith where the Prophet said 'this is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer.' The Hanafi response systematically deconstructs this argument by questioning the authenticity of the hadith, its evidentiary weight as an ahad report, and the scope of its demonstrative reference. Understanding this refutation sharpens your ability to evaluate hadith-based arguments in fiqh and highlights the Hanafi method of istidlal.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i argument
Understand the opposing claim: tartib is fard because the Prophet performed wudu in order and stated that prayer is only accepted with such wudu.
The hadith: 'هذا وضوء لا يقبل الله صلاة إلا به' (This is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer).
2
Evaluate the hadith's authenticity
Check the chains of narration. Major hadith scholars (al-Zayla'i, Ibn Hajar, al-Nawawi) declared the hadith weak (da'if) in all its chains.
Weak narrators like Musayyib ibn Wadih are present. The hadith is not fit for establishing obligation.
3
Apply Hanafi usul on ahad hadith
Even if the hadith were authentic, it is an ahad report. In Hanafi usul, ahad reports do not establish fard (obligation) unless they are reinforced by other evidence.
Fard requires qat'i thubut and qat'i dalala; ahad gives zann only.
4
Scrutinize the pronoun reference
The demonstrative 'this' (هذا) in the hadith does not necessarily refer to the order. The Hanafi commentator argues it refers specifically to washing once each (al-marrah), not to other attributes like order, starting side, or continuity.
If 'this' referred to all attributes, it would necessitate that muwalat and tayammun are also fard, which the Shafi'is do not claim.
5
Test logical consistency
Apply reductio ad absurdum: if the hadith proved order fard, it would also prove muwalat and starting with the right as fard, leading to a position the opponent rejects.
This demonstrates the weakness of the Shafi'i inference.

And this wudu was performed in order, so tartib is fard. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed wudu once each and said: 'This is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer.' Then he performed wudu twice each and said: 'This is the wudu of one whose reward is doubled.' Then he performed wudu thrice each and said: 'This is my wudu and the wudu of the messengers before me.' Al-Bayhaqi also narrated it, and in its chain is Musayyib ibn Wadih who is not reliable. Similarly, Ibn Majah, al-Tabarani in his al-Mu'jam al-Awsat, Ibn Hibban in Kitab al-Du'afa', and al-Daraqutni in Kitab Ghara'ib Malik narrated it, and all its chains are weak, as elaborated by al-Zayla'i, al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar, al-Nawawi, and others. [1] His statement: 'so tartib is fard' means that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed wudu once each—i.e., he washed his limbs once each—and said: 'This—i.e., what I have done—is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer.' So he restricted acceptance of prayer to his wudu, and his wudu was performed in order, so it is understood that Allah does not accept prayer except with wudu performed in order. And what is like that cannot be except obligatory, so tartib is fard. This reasoning is refuted in several ways: 1. The hadith in all its chains is weak and not suitable to be used as proof for something being obligatory. 2. Even if it were authentic, it is ahad reports which do not establish obligation. 3. The claim that that wudu was performed in order is a claim without evidence, for it has not been reported in the chains of the mentioned hadith nor is it found in hadith books. And what they transmitted in some chain... And I have a good answer: that he performed wudu once each and said: 'This is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer,' so this statement refers only to the number of times (once), not to other things. Because this wudu is either started from the right or from the left, and also either with continuous sequence (muwalat) or without. So his statement 'This wudu...' to the end, if it refers to this wudu with all its attributes, then it would necessitate the obligation of muwalat or its opposite, and the obligation of starting from the right or its opposite. And if it does not refer to the wudu with all its attributes, then it does not indicate the obligation of tartib. Their books state that he performed wudu in order and said: 'This is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer.' And al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar in Takhrij Ahadith al-Rafi'i and others explicitly said: 'It has no basis.' Among them is what occurred to the commentator, the gist of which: we concede that his wudu was performed in order, but we say: the indication by 'this' refers only to the number of times (once), not to others. Because his wudu is either started from the right or the left, and either with muwalat or without. So his statement 'this' if it refers to that wudu with all its attributes, then it would necessitate the obligation of muwalat or its absence, and the obligation of starting from the right or the left, which is contrary to their school. And if it does not refer to the wudu with all its attributes, then it does not indicate the obligation of tartib. And the claim that what is referred to is the attribute of tartib to the exclusion of others is not supported by evidence. Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary on the chapter of taharah, specifically on the issue of tartib (order) in wudu. The author first presents the argument that tartib is fard (obligatory), based on a hadith narrated by al-Bayhaqi and others. The hadith describes the Prophet performing wudu once each, twice each, and thrice each, with statements about acceptance of prayer and reward. The argument is that since the Prophet's wudu was performed in order, and he said prayer is only accepted with such wudu, tartib becomes obligatory. The author then refutes this reasoning with several points. First, the hadith is weak in all its chains, as pointed out by major hadith scholars. Second, even if authentic, it is a hadith ahad, which does not establish obligation in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. Third, there is no evidence that the Prophet's wudu in that hadith was performed in order; this is an unsubstantiated claim. The author then presents an additional response: the Prophet's statement 'this wudu' refers only to the act of washing once each (the number of times), not to other attributes like order, starting side, or continuity. If it were taken to include all attributes, it would also imply obligation of muwalat and starting from the right, which even the opponents do not hold as obligatory. Thus, the hadith does not prove tartib as fard. This is a classic inter-madhhab dispute where the Hanafis reject the Shafi'i reliance on this hadith for tartib. The Hanafi position is that tartib is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard, based on stronger evidence.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): Performing the actions of wudu in a specific order: washing face, then hands, then wiping head, then washing feet.
الموالاة (al-muwalat): Performing the actions of wudu consecutively without undue delay.
التيامن (al-tayammun): Starting with the right side (e.g., washing right hand before left).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, why does the hadith 'هذا وضوء لا يقبل الله صلاة إلا به' not prove that tartib is fard?
A) Because the hadith is weak and even if authentic, the pronoun 'هذا' refers only to the number of times (once), not to order.
B) Because the hadith is mutawatir and establishes obligation of order.
C) Because the hadith proves that wudu must be done three times each.
D) Because the hadith is about wudu of the prophets, not about obligation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi refutation of tartib as fard rests on three pillars: the hadith's weakness, its ahad nature, and the limited reference of the pronoun 'this'.

Refuting the Shafi'i Objection on the Hadith of Wudu
Hanafi critical response to a Shafi'i argument about wudu hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the hadith 'this wudu' does not prove the obligation of tartib, and evaluate al-Dawani's counter-argument.

Core Idea
A demonstrative reference to an entire action cannot prove any single attribute without additional evidence.

The Shafi'i school argues that the Prophet's statement 'this is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer' proves that tartib (order) is obligatory in wudu. The Hanafi response is a masterclass in usul al-lughah (linguistic principles) and naqd (critique). This passage unpacks the hermeneutic fallacy of narrowing a general reference to a specific attribute. You will learn how the same logic that Shafi'is use for tartib would force them to accept other attributes they reject, exposing the weakness of their proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i claim
What is the Shafi'i argument for the obligation of tartib based on this hadith? They claim that since the Prophet performed wudu in order and then said 'this wudu', the order is included in the reference.
The opposing school is represented by Jalal al-Din al-Dawani.
2
Analyze the Hanafi critique
How does the Hanafi commentator use the concept that 'this wudu' had multiple attributes (washing once, starting right/left, with/without muwalat) to refute specificity to tartib? He argues that if it proved one attribute, it would prove all, which the Shafi'is do not accept.
The demonstrative 'hadha' refers to the entire act, not a single part.
3
Evaluate al-Dawani's defense
Al-Dawani tries to salvage the Shafi'i position by suggesting that the Prophet may have started with the left to show permissibility of tayammun, or started with the right but that does not prove obligation. How does this attempt to limit the reference?
He uses the attribute of starting with the right/left to show the hadith does not prove obligation of tayammun.
4
Apply the Hanafi rebuttal
The commentator shows that al-Dawani's same reasoning applies to tartib: if the hadith does not prove obligation of tayammun because it could be permissive, then it also does not prove obligation of tartib because it could be permissive.
This exposes the inconsistency in the Shafi'i position.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد سَنَحَ لي جواب حَسَن ، وهو أَنَّهُ توضأ مرة مرة ، وقال : «هَذَا وُضُوءٌ لَا يَقْبَلُ اللهُ الصَّلاةَ إِلا بِهِ ، فهذا القولُ يرجع إلى المرَّة فحسب، لا إلى الأشياء الأخر؛ لأنَّ هذا الوضوء لا يخلو : إما أن يكون ابتداؤه من اليمين، أو من اليسار. وأيضاً : إما أن يكون على سبيل الموالاة، أو عدمها. فقوله : «هَذَا وُضُوء... إلى آخرِه ، إن أريد به هذا الوضوء بجميع أوصافه يلزمُ فرضية الموالاة، أو ضدّها ، أو التيامن أو ضدّه ، وإن لم يُرِدْ بجميع أوصافه لا يدلُّ على فرضيَّةِ الترتيب. كتبهم أنه توضأ مرتباً وقال : هذا وضوء لا يقبلُ الله صلاة إلا به، وقد صرَّحَ الحافظ ابن حجر في تخريج أحاديث الرافعي، وغيره : «إنّه لا أصل له». ومنها : ما ظهر للشارح، وحاصله : أنا سلّمنا أنّ وضوءه ذلك كان مرتباً، لكنَّا نقول : الإشارة بهذا يرجع إلى المرّة فقط لا إلى غيره، وذلك لأن وضوءه ذلك لا يخلو إما أن يكون ابتداءً الأركان فيه من اليمين أو من اليسار، وكذلك لا يخلو إما أن يكون بالموالاة أو بتركها. فقوله : «هذا إن كان إشارة إلى ذلك الوضوء بجميع أوصافه تلزم فرضيَّة الموالاة أو عدمها، وفرضيته التيامن أو التياسر ، وهو خلافُ مذهبهم أيضاً، وإن لم يكن إشارة إلى الوضوء بجميع أوصافه لم يدلُّ على افتراض الترتيب، ودعوى أنَّ المشار إليه هو وصف الترتيب لا غيره لم يدل عليها دليل. قوله : أو التيامن ... الخ ؛ قال جلال الدين محمد بن أسعد الدواني له في رسالته «أنموذج العلوم» ناصراً لمذهبه ومجيباً عن إيراد الشارح له، أقول : «يمكن أن لعله تياسر في هذا الوضوء لبيان الجواز وعدم وجوب التياسر معلوم من الروايات الصحيحة الشائعة، أو نختار أنه لعله تيامن وعدم وجوب التيامن معلوم من سائر أحواله وأقواله». انتهى. أقول : قد خفي على هذا المحقق في الفنون العقلية أن مثل هذا الكلام جارٍ في الترتيب أيضاً.
And there occurred to me a good answer, which is that he performed wudu washing each limb once, and said: 'This is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer.' So this statement refers only to the (washing) once, not to other matters; because this wudu is not free: either its beginning is from the right or from the left. Also: either it is with continuity (muwalat) or without it. So his statement: 'This is wudu...' etc., if by it he meant this wudu with all its attributes, then it would necessitate the obligation of muwalat or its opposite, and of starting with the right or its opposite. And if he did not mean all its attributes, then it does not indicate the obligation of tartib. It is written in their books that he performed wudu in order and said: 'This is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer.' But al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar in his Takhrij Ahadith al-Rafi'i and others stated: 'It has no basis.' And among them is what appeared to the commentator, and its summary: we concede that his wudu was ordered, but we say: the reference with 'this' refers only to the (washing) once, not to other matters. That is because his wudu is not free: either the beginning of the parts is from the right or from the left, and likewise it is not free either from muwalat or its omission. So his statement: 'This' if it is a reference to that wudu with all its attributes, then the obligation of muwalat or its opposite, and the obligation of starting with the right or the left would follow, which is also contrary to their school. And if it is not a reference to the wudu with all its attributes, then it does not indicate the obligation of tartib. And the claim that what is referred to is the attribute of tartib and not others is not supported by evidence. His statement: 'or starting with the right...etc.' Jalal al-Din Muhammad ibn As'ad al-Dawani said in his treatise 'Anmudhaj al-'Ulum' supporting his school and responding to the commentator's objection: I say: 'It is possible that he started with the left in this wudu to show permissibility, and the non-obligation of starting with the right is known from authentic and widespread narrations. Or we choose that he started with the right, and the non-obligation of starting with the right is known from his other states and statements.' End. I say: This researcher in the intellectual sciences has overlooked that such a statement also applies to tartib.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute, specifically a Hanafi critical response to a Shafi'i objection. The Shafi'i school uses the hadith 'this is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer' to argue for the obligation of tartib (order) in wudu. The Hanafi commentator refutes this by focusing on the demonstrative 'this' (hadha). He argues that the Prophet's wudu had multiple attributes: washing each limb once, starting from the right or left, with or without muwalat. Pointing to 'this wudu' without specification cannot prove all attributes are obligatory; it only proves the attribute of washing once, which is common to all those possibilities. The Shafi'i scholar al-Dawani tries to salvage the hadith by suggesting the Prophet intentionally started with the left to show permissibility. But the Hanafi rebuts that the same argument could be applied to tartib, undermining the Shafi'i position. Thus, the hadith does not establish the obligation of tartib.

Key Terms
المرة (al-marra): Washing each limb once, as opposed to three times.
الترتيب (al-tartib): Performing the actions of wudu in the order mentioned in the Quran (face, hands, head, feet).
التيامن (al-tayammun): Starting with the right side in wudu (e.g., washing right hand before left).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi refutation, what does the Prophet's statement 'this is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer' primarily prove?
A) The obligation of tartib (order)
B) The obligation of washing each limb once
C) The obligation of muwalat (continuity)
D) The obligation of starting with the right

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'this wudu' refers to the entire act and cannot be used to prove the obligation of any specific attribute like tartib without additional evidence.

Definition of Wala' in Wudu and Its Evidence
Defining al-wala' and citing hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of al-wala' (succession) in wudu and explain its legal implication based on the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Al-wala' requires washing wudu limbs successively without drying — its violation necessitates repeating the entire wudu.

This lesson defines the key concept of al-wala' (succession) in wudu, a point of difference among madhahib. The Hanafi school holds it as wajib. Understanding this definition is crucial for correct wudu practice. The passage clarifies the meaning and provides hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the term al-wala' linguistically and legally
Start with the linguistic meaning: 'succession' (tataabu'). Then move to the legal definition: succession in the essential parts of wudu without drying of a limb under normal conditions.
The term is interchangeable with al-muwalat.
2
Note the condition of no drying under normal circumstances
The definition specifies 'with moderate air and moderate body' — meaning normal environmental and physical conditions. Extreme heat or cold may affect the ruling.
This condition is important for practical application.
3
Recognize the commentator's deficiency and the resolution
The passage notes that the commentator's definition only mentions washing (ghusl), excluding wiping (masah) of the head. The author resolves this by interpreting 'ghusl' in a broad sense covering both literal washing and legal wiping.
This shows Hanafi precision in defining legal terms.
4
Analyze the hadith proof and its implication
The hadith from Abu Dawood: The Prophet saw a man praying with a dry spot on his foot and ordered him to repeat wudu and prayer. This indicates that if a part is left dry, the entire wudu must be repeated, implying the obligation of continuous washing (wala').
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning (dalala) is considered qat'i by the Hanafis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1]قوله : والولاء ؛ بكسر الواو والمد ، بمعنى : التتابع، وهو عبارة عن التتابع في أركان الوضوء من غير أن يتخللها جفافُ عضو مع ا اعتدال الهواء واعتدال البدن، وأما تفسير الشارح فلا يخلو عن مساحة ؛ لعدم شموله مسح الرأس إلا أن يقال : أراد : بالغسل أعم من الحقيقي والحكمي. وقد أخرج أبو داود في سننه: «أنه رأى رجلاً يصلي وفي قدمه لمعة لم يصبها الماء، فأمره أن يعيد الوضوء والصلاة» (۳)، وأخرج ابن أبي شيبة وعبد الرزاق :
[1] His statement: 'al-wala' – with kasra of the waw and madd, meaning succession (tataabu'), and it is an expression of succession in the essential parts of wudu such that there does not occur drying of a limb considering moderate air and moderate body. As for the commentator's interpretation, it is not free from deficiency because it does not include wiping the head, unless it is said that he intended by 'ghusl' the general sense including both literal and legal washing. Abu Dawood in his Sunan narrated that he saw a man praying with a spot on his foot not touched by water, so he ordered him to repeat wudu and prayer. And Ibn Abi Shayba and Abd al-Razzaq narrated...
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage provides the definition of al-wala' (succession) in wudu. This is a ruling definition. The term means performing the actions of wudu successively such that a previous limb does not dry before washing the next, assuming moderate air and body temperature. The commentator (sharih) is critiqued for an incomplete interpretation because his definition only mentions ghusl (washing) and does not cover masah (wiping the head). However, this can be resolved by taking 'ghusl' in a general sense that includes both literal washing and legal wiping. The passage then cites a hadith from Abu Dawood: the Prophet saw a man praying with a dry spot on his foot and ordered him to repeat both wudu and prayer. This hadith implies that if a limb dries before the next is washed, the wudu is incomplete, thus establishing the requirement of wala' (or at least its importance). The names of Ibn Abi Shayba and Abd al-Razzaq are mentioned as additional narrators.

Key Terms
الولاء (al-wala'): Succession in the essential parts of wudu, ensuring no limb dries before washing the next under normal conditions.
الموالاة (al-muwalat): The same as al-wala'; performing wudu actions consecutively.
التتابع (al-tatabu'): Succession; one after another without interruption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Washing each limb three times
B) Performing wudu in the order of the Quranic verse
C) Washing limbs successively without drying of a previous limb under normal conditions
D) Using fresh water for each limb

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines al-wala' as wajib succession without drying, as supported by the hadith ordering repetition when a part is dry.

The Ruling of Continuity (al-Wala') in Wudu: Hanafi vs Maliki
Inter-madhhab dispute on the obligation of continuity in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that al-wala' is sunnah and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument using the concept of ahad hadith.

Core Idea
Continuity in wudu is sunnah, not fard: isolated reports cannot establish obligation against silence of Quran and mutawatir.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute: whether continuity (al-wala') in wudu is obligatory or merely recommended. The Hanafi school argues it is sunnah, while the Maliki school holds it is fard. The debate hinges on the strength of the evidence—particularly the hadith of the man with the dry spot and the practice of Ibn Umar. By studying this dispute, you will understand how Hanafi usul principles (e.g., ahad hadith cannot establish fard) shape fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Define al-wala' and identify the contested ruling
Read the author's definition of al-wala' and note its conditions. Understand that the dispute is whether this continuity is obligatory (fard) or merely sunnah.
The definition includes 'no drying of a limb under normal conditions'.
2
Present the opponent's (Maliki) evidence
The Maliki school relies on the hadith of the man with the dry spot (Abu Dawud) and Umar's command to repeat wudu. Identify why these are used to claim obligation.
The command to repeat wudu is seen as proof of a missing obligation.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) the reports are ahad (isolated), which cannot establish fard; (2) the command to repeat is consistent with strengthening a sunnah. Grasp the usul principle that ahad reports do not create obligation when the Quran and mutawatir are silent.
The author also cites Ibn Umar's practice (wiping over khuffs after a break) to show that continuity is not required.
4
Evaluate the practical consequence
Contrast the thamarah al-khilaf: In the Hanafi school, wudu is valid even if continuity is broken (though makruh). In the Maliki school, it is invalid and must be repeated. Understand how this affects daily practice.
This difference matters when someone inadvertently delays washing between limbs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة الوضوء والولاء
والولاء) : أي غسلُ الأعضاء المفروضات على سبيلِ التَّعاقب بحيثُ لا يَجِفُ العضو الأول.
يقال لعله تياسر في هذا الوضوء لبيان الجواز وعدم وجوب التياسر معلوم من الروايات الصحيحة الشائعة، أو نختار أنه لعله تيامن وعدم وجوب التيامن معلوم من سائر أحواله وأقواله». انتهى.
أقول : قد خفي على هذا المحقق في الفنون العقلية أن مثل هذا الكلام جارٍ في الترتيب أيضاً.
قوله : والولاء ؛ بكسر الواو والمد ، بمعنى : التتابع، وهو عبارة عن التتابع في أركان الوضوء من غير أن يتخللها جفافُ عضو مع اعتدال الهواء واعتدال البدن(۱) ، وأما تفسير الشارح فلا يخلو عن مساحة ؛ لعدم شموله مسح الرأس إلا أن يقال : أراد : بالغسل أعم من الحقيقي والحكمي. وقد أخرج أبو داود في سننه: «أنه رأى رجلاً يصلي وفي قدمه لمعة لم يصبها الماء، فأمره أن يعيد الوضوء والصلاة» (۳)، وأخرج ابن أبي شيبة وعبد الرزاق : أن عمر رأى رجلاً توضأ فبقي في رجله قدر ظفر فقال: أعد الوضوء»، ونحوه في «مسند الإمام أحمد». وبهذا استند مالك في افتراض الولاء ، وليس بصحيح، فإنّ هذه أخبار آحاد لا تثبت الافتراض مع كون القرآن والأحاديث المشهورة ساكتة عنه ، على أن الأمر بالإعادة يستقيم على تقدير السنية أيضاً، اهتماماً بشأن السنن. وقد أخرج مالك في «الموطأ» : «إنّ ابن عمر توضأ فغسل وجهه ويديه ومسح برأسه، ثم دعي بجنازة ليصلي عليها حين دخل المسجد، فمسح على خفيه وهذا نص على عدم كون الولاء فرضاً.
قوله : من غير دليل على فرضيّتها ؛ إنّما زاد هذا لئلا يرد أنه قد واظب على الفرائض كالصلاة والصوم فيلزم أن تكون سنة، والمراد بالافتراض ما يشمل الوجوب أيضا. فحاصله : أنَّ المواظبة إنّما تدلّ على السنيّة إذا لم يدلّ دليل آخر على كون ذلك الأمر الذي واظب عليه فرضاً أو واجباً، وهذه الأمور المذكورة كذلك، والمراد بالمواظبة المداومة مع الترك أحياناً كما سيصرح به في تعريف السنة. فإن قلت : قد مرَّ أنّ بعض الأئمة ذهبوا إلى افتراض بعض الأشياء المذكورة، وأقاموا عليه الأدلة، فلا يصح قوله : «من غير دليل على فرضيتها». قلت : لما كانت الدلائل المذكورة مقدوحة عندنا جعل وجودها كالعدم.
Book of Purification: Wudu and Continuity. (Continuity) means washing the prescribed limbs consecutively such that the first limb does not dry. It is said that perhaps he turned left in this wudu to indicate permissibility, and the non-obligation of turning left is known from sound widespread narrations, or we choose that perhaps he turned right and the non-obligation of turning right is known from his other states and statements. End. I say: This investigator in intellectual sciences overlooked that such speech also applies to sequence. His statement: 'And continuity' with a kasra on the waw and madd, meaning succession, which is succession in the pillars of wudu without dryness of a limb occurring in between under moderate air and body temperature. The commentator's interpretation is not free of ease because it does not include wiping the head unless one says he meant washing in a general sense including real and legal. Abu Dawud narrated in his Sunan that he saw a man praying with a spot on his foot that water had not reached, so he ordered him to repeat wudu and prayer. Ibn Abi Shaybah and Abd al-Razzaq narrated that Umar saw a man who performed wudu and a spot the size of a nail remained on his foot, so he said: 'Repeat the wudu', and similar in Musnad Ahmad. Based on this, Malik held that continuity is obligatory, but this is not correct, for these are isolated reports that cannot establish obligation, especially since the Quran and well-known hadith are silent about it, and the command to repeat is consistent with it being sunnah out of concern for sunan. Malik narrated in al-Muwatta that Ibn Umar performed wudu, washed his face and hands and wiped his head, then he was called for a funeral prayer upon entering the mosque, so he wiped over his khuffs—this is clear text that continuity is not obligatory. His statement: 'without proof of its being obligatory' was added only to prevent the objection that he regularly performed the obligations like prayer and fasting, which would necessitate that they be sunnah. The intention of 'obligation' includes wajib as well. The gist is that regularity indicates sunnah only if no other evidence indicates that the action is fard or wajib, and these mentioned actions are such. Regularity means continuous practice with occasional abandonment, as will be clarified in the definition of sunnah. If you say: Some imams held that some of these things are obligatory and adduced proofs, so his statement 'without proof of its being obligatory' is incorrect. I say: Since the mentioned proofs are considered weak in our view, their existence is like non-existence.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling of continuity (al-wala') in wudu. The author begins by defining al-wala' as washing the prescribed limbs consecutively such that the first limb does not dry before finishing, under normal conditions. He then quotes a hadith from Abu Dawud and an athar from Umar where the Prophet and Umar ordered a person to repeat wudu and prayer due to a missed spot. Imam Malik used these as evidence to declare al-wala' fard (obligatory). The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) These are ahad reports, which cannot establish obligation (fard/wajib) because the Quran and mutawatir hadith are silent; (2) The command to repeat can be interpreted as a strong recommendation (sunnah) to emphasize the sunnah's importance, not to indicate obligation. The passage further strengthens the Hanafi position by citing a narration from Malik's own Muwatta: Ibn Umar, after performing wudu, did not immediately pray but wiped over his khuffs when called for a funeral, showing that a break (jumping from washing to wiping) was considered permissible, which contradicts the requirement of sequence. The author also addresses a potential objection: if the Prophet regularly performed something, could it be concluded as sunnah even if it is actually fard? He clarifies that regularity indicates sunnah only when there is no independent proof of obligation, and the Hanafi view is that such proofs (for al-wala' being fard) are weak. Thus, the Hanafi position is that al-wala' is sunnah, not fard or wajib.

Key Terms
الولاء (al-walā'): Continuity in wudu: washing the limbs consecutively without the first drying under normal conditions.
السنة (al-sunnah): An action that the Prophet performed regularly but occasionally left, without evidence of obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of al-wala' (continuity) in wudu?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that continuity in wudu is sunnah because ahad hadith cannot establish fard against the silence of the Quran and mutawatir.
